  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_829c7c93-feaa-4deb-b1b8-74409ca86e92'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer3421826130427262015">In the days before the Civil War, there lived in New Orleans the gens de couleur libre - copper-skinned half-castes, liberated by their owners, but confined by their color to a life of political nonexistence and social subordination. Still, an aristocracy would emerge in this society: artist, poets, and musicians, plantation owners, scientists and craftsmen whose talents a</span>
  <span id="freeText3421826130427262015" style="display:none">In the days before the Civil War, there lived in New Orleans the gens de couleur libre - copper-skinned half-castes, liberated by their owners, but confined by their color to a life of political nonexistence and social subordination. Still, an aristocracy would emerge in this society: artist, poets, and musicians, plantation owners, scientists and craftsmen whose talents and reputations would extend far beyond the limits of their small world. <br /><br />Mega-selling author Anne Rice's probing, lyrical style sweeps us into their midst as she introduces Marcel, the sensitive, blue-eyed scholar, Marie, his breathtakingly beautiful sister, whose curse is to pass for white; Christophe, novelist and teacher, the idol of all young gens and stunning Anna Bella, whose allure for the well-to-do white man would become legend.<br /><br />Here is a compelling and richly textured tale of a people forever caught in the shadows between black and white.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3421826130427262015" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Popular Answered Questions

<div id='communityQuestionsWithAnswers'>
<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1266270-i-love-this-book-i-said-in-my-brief">I LOVE this book. I said in my brief review that it is like art. Rice writes so well it takes my breath away. 
But I wonder, how much of this story is true? I have tried Googling it, and to no avail. Is this a made up or exaggerated story? Or did this kind of thing really happen in New Orleans? I mean I understand the actual characters are fiction. I just mean in general.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1266270'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F43798.The_Feast_of_All_Saints">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1266270-i-love-this-book-i-said-in-my-brief">2 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1266270-i-love-this-book-i-said-in-my-brief">See all 3 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/2579244-leonide-martin"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1544815904i/2579244._UX100_CR0,4,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/2579244-leonide-martin">Leonide Martin</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I was born in New Orleans and raised in southern Louisiana. From everything I know, Rice's portrayal of New Orleans culture in the mid-1800s is quite <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I was born in New Orleans and raised in southern Louisiana. From everything I know, Rice's portrayal of New Orleans culture in the mid-1800s is quite accurate. It's true that free blacks owned plantations in Louisiana, and owned slaves who worked there. It's true that wealthy white planters kept mulatto mistresses and had families in the city. The quadroon balls actually took place for many years. What was so touching was the angst suffered by free men of color such as protagonist Marcel. That was a revelation just because I'd never explored their experiences at the time. I'm convinced Rice's portrayal is accurate.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerFooter'>

<div id="review_197419030" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/197419030" />
    <a title="Aleeda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4876884-aleeda"><img alt="Aleeda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459203953p2/4876884.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/197419030?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aleeda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aleeda" href="/user/show/4876884-aleeda">Aleeda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345334534" href="/book/show/6417357-the-feast-of-all-saints">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer197419030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12743817771493606890">This novel so often gets overlooked; Anne Rice's mystical writings about vampires, mummies and witches easily overshadow it. Pity, because for my money, this is her BEST work. While researching Interview with a Vampire, she gathered enough information, for this, her second novel (as Anne Rice). The book blends a wonderful love of a beautiful city (New Orleans) with a genuine interest in African American culture. The gens de couleur libre, a society of free middle-class mixed-raced people, had co</span>
  <span id="freeText12743817771493606890" style="display:none">This novel so often gets overlooked; Anne Rice's mystical writings about vampires, mummies and witches easily overshadow it. Pity, because for my money, this is her BEST work. While researching Interview with a Vampire, she gathered enough information, for this, her second novel (as Anne Rice). The book blends a wonderful love of a beautiful city (New Orleans) with a genuine interest in African American culture. The gens de couleur libre, a society of free middle-class mixed-raced people, had codified rules which were obeyed and respected, for the most part, by the wealthy slaveholders, and their interracial families. They had balls in which the slaveholders pursuedtheir mistresses, and by Ms. Rice's accounts, established a second family in which the father paid for the support and education of his children. The gens de couleur has their own doctors, lawyers, and professionals of all kinds. The white and black societies had a separate but symbiotic class structure, with each knowing his role.This is an overlooked part of history and the story has been told in a sensitive, imaginative way by Ms. Rice. I loved the book so much, I sought out a hardcover copy for my library...Top 25!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12743817771493606890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_170956911" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Jen Pavich" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5141099-jen-pavich"><img alt="Jen Pavich" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300392608p2/5141099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170956911?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen Pavich" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen Pavich" href="/user/show/5141099-jen-pavich">Jen Pavich</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170956911" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1534004903967925695">Completely different than most Anne Rice novels, this one forgoes the supernatural entirely. <br/><br/>One of my favorite books, this novel is rich with history of pre-Civil War New Orleans and rural Louisiana. Characters are very compelling and Rice deftly explores the nearly mind boggling complexity of race and relationships in a city where degrees of black- or whiteness meant everything.<br/><br/>NOTE: The movie was flat and much oversimplified by comparison, not even worth watching.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7769548073347036955">I love books that highlight African American history, and I was beside myself when i found this book one day in a bin at Goodwill. For .25 I got one of the best books I've ever read. Mrs. Rice weaves an excellent tale about the gen de libre coloure, a little known community of mixed races free people of color that populated Louisiana. I was completely draw into the world of Marcel St. Marie as he struggled with his identity on his road to becoming a man.<br/><br/>This was a great book.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1399737364" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1399737364" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/635367-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1197426957p2/635367.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1399737364?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/635367-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1399737364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10980371012526714574">This is the third time I've read this novel. The first, at a tender age of 15, left me wrecked, changed, broken hearted and overwhelmed. I then spent a summer a couple years later reading it aloud to my aunt, who made fun of my French pronunciation as well as added sound effects when necessary (a specialty of hers, learned from many years of listening to me read to her). The second reading cemented my youthful longing for an intelligent man and a journey to the city of light. Now, more than two </span>
  <span id="freeText10980371012526714574" style="display:none">This is the third time I've read this novel. The first, at a tender age of 15, left me wrecked, changed, broken hearted and overwhelmed. I then spent a summer a couple years later reading it aloud to my aunt, who made fun of my French pronunciation as well as added sound effects when necessary (a specialty of hers, learned from many years of listening to me read to her). The second reading cemented my youthful longing for an intelligent man and a journey to the city of light. Now, more than two decades later, I've returned to The Feast of All Saints out of curiosity. Only the occasional drift beyond the border and into the purple land of too-flowery prose kept me from assigning 5 stars to this novel. Despite many (many!) other "preternatural" novels by Rice that I have loved or have at least enjoyed, this historical novel about a boy coming of age in a cruel, difficult way is by far my favorite. The drama is intense, of course--how could it not be, with a 14 year old narrator with passionate ideas about art and music and Paris? Someone cries on nearly every page. I should, of course, be an adult and turn my nose up at this. But I refuse. This novel made me realize at a young age that your dreams are not awarded to you, but that you must work to make them come true. It taught me that love is illusory and must be experienced, cherished in every form that it appears. It taught me not to believe in anything and to never stop believing in everything. This is a big, contradictory, romantic, preposterous and wonderful novel that I still love. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10980371012526714574" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer73877597" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11130644583913381056">I'm giving this five stars (it was amazing) because that is how I felt about this book when I read it when I was fifteen. My dad bought this book for me on one of our Sunday bookstore browsing days and I picked it up only because I liked the cover. I had never heard of Anne Rice and didn't know anything about her Vampire Chronicles. <br/><br/>I was immediately sucked into this book by its historical context,intricate plot, kind of naughtiness, and very romantic New Orleans setting. I was devastated at the</span>
  <span id="freeText11130644583913381056" style="display:none">I'm giving this five stars (it was amazing) because that is how I felt about this book when I read it when I was fifteen. My dad bought this book for me on one of our Sunday bookstore browsing days and I picked it up only because I liked the cover. I had never heard of Anne Rice and didn't know anything about her Vampire Chronicles. <br /><br />I was immediately sucked into this book by its historical context,intricate plot, kind of naughtiness, and very romantic New Orleans setting. I was devastated at the end because it really leaves you hanging. I've waited all these years for Anne to write a sequel and tell me what happened to Marcel. I doubt she ever will.<br /><br />I'm curious if the five stars would hold up if I were to re-read this today. I might have to try that soon.</span>

<div id="review_3002357591" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3002357591" />
    <a title="Kym Moore" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12839345-kym-moore"><img alt="Kym Moore" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358115990p2/12839345.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3002357591?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kym Moore" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kym Moore" href="/user/show/12839345-kym-moore">Kym Moore</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/159497.The_Feast_of_All_Saints">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3002357591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer173498033938975694">This is a fist clenching, hyperventilating, teeth grinding story that was an epic piece of work by Anne Rice. She is typically best known for her vampire-themed works but did an incredible job in her storytelling of the tragedies, false identities, and identity crisis affecting so many lives in Louisiana, with this fictional period piece. Yet, Rice included non-fictional events woven into this storyline to reveal those ugly and monstrous truths many tried to hide in the history of this country t</span>
  <span id="freeText173498033938975694" style="display:none">This is a fist clenching, hyperventilating, teeth grinding story that was an epic piece of work by Anne Rice. She is typically best known for her vampire-themed works but did an incredible job in her storytelling of the tragedies, false identities, and identity crisis affecting so many lives in Louisiana, with this fictional period piece. Yet, Rice included non-fictional events woven into this storyline to reveal those ugly and monstrous truths many tried to hide in the history of this country that could also be found in countries around the world.<br /><br />A false sense of security, illusions of all the accoutrements of a family, but no family...illusions of all the accoutrements of a gentleman but not a gentleman...illusions of all the accoutrements of wealth but no wealth. Quadroons, some thought to be white still had the blood of color in them, were always reminded that they were going to always be people of color living in a white man's world.<br /><br />Even those who were free people of color (gens de couleur libre) were still considered inferior to the white man. Injustice separated the prosperous gens de couleur (who struggled to be fully enfranchised) from their white fellowmen. They have been caught between the worlds of privilege and oppression, master and slave.<br /><br />The rich and privileged have taken advantage of the weak and lowly, with their selfishness and explicit lusts, exploiting them in no uncertain terms, having their way when it is convenient. I'd hoped for a more happy ending for all of those who fell victim by default. Sadly, this was a harsh reality during this period piece of our time and country. I wish things ended better for Marcel, Marie, Richard, Christophe, and Anna Belle, but as tragic as the storyline went, I believe they survived from those tragic mistakes adults made and the consequences they had to deal with as a result of those salacious mistakes.<br /><br />My hats off to Anne Rice for a story that was filled with a myriad of emotions (anger, surprises, intrigue, sadness, hope, happiness and survival). This is a recommended read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="173498033938975694" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_255843661" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/255843661" />
    <a title="Jessica Thurlow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7327893-jessica-thurlow"><img alt="Jessica Thurlow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438041031p2/7327893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/255843661?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Thurlow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Thurlow" href="/user/show/7327893-jessica-thurlow">Jessica Thurlow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer255843661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15245495547074719416">Feast of all Saints: A Refreshing Fiction<br/>I have been a fan of Anne Rice since I was twelve years old. I t was then that Lestat held me in his arms and whispered sweet nothings in my ear. And it is becuse of this experience that the name Rice has become synonymous with all things preternatural for me. Thus, I was shocked to find, when I began reading The Feast of all Saints that the novel contained no elements of the supernatural save for a few instances of spiritual awakening. I confess that I w</span>
  <span id="freeText15245495547074719416" style="display:none">Feast of all Saints: A Refreshing Fiction<br />I have been a fan of Anne Rice since I was twelve years old. I t was then that Lestat held me in his arms and whispered sweet nothings in my ear. And it is becuse of this experience that the name Rice has become synonymous with all things preternatural for me. Thus, I was shocked to find, when I began reading The Feast of all Saints that the novel contained no elements of the supernatural save for a few instances of spiritual awakening. I confess that I was a wee bit concerned that I wouldn’t like this more serious version of Ms. Rice. I was trepidatious – would this novel break my heart?<br /><br />I’ve been reading it for ages. Not because it was hard to read but because I was worried I wouldn’t like it and I simply didn’t want to have to change my perception of the awe-inspiring Ms. Rice. Eventually, I summoned the strength and dove headlong into the creole world that lives within the pages of this book. Knowing virtually nothing about the gens de couleur libre, I made exciting and sometimes horrifying discoveries with every page.<br /><br />This book is drastically different from The Vampire Chronicles - as it should be. Those books, along with a few others I’ve read by Rice, make comments on society and human nature often in a very subtle way. They gently whisper these ideas and the ideas become apparent after you’ve read them – they become intertwined and inseparable from the story and yet still vivid. With this book, Rice has taken a much more direct path. The ideas are very often literally, shouted at the reader by various characters. Revelations about racism and gender inequality are frequent and I found myself dog-earring many a page so that I might return to the passage to savour the intensity and eloquence of the words.<br /><br />One particular outburst will stay with me for always. It doesn’t directly link to either racism or gender equality but touches a matter quite close to my heart – the importance of literature. When I first read this passage, I nearly shouted out loud: someone else was able to articulate just how I felt about the written word – the idea that it keeps the thoughts and ideas they embody alive forever, that books should be treated almost like living things. This is what Marcel had to say:<br /><br />“My teacher, Monsieur De Latte … handles books as if they<br /><br />were dead! …. My teacher believes in those books only<br /><br />because they occupy space …. I want to know what’s inside<br /><br />of them … what they actually mean. We forget all the time,<br /><br />I think. that things are made, that this table was made by<br /><br />someone for instance, with hammer and nails, and that<br /><br />what’s in books was made by someone, someone flesh and<br /><br />blood like ourselves wrote those lines, they were alive,<br /><br />they might have gone this way or that with a<br /><br />different word …. I think, Monsieur, people forget this …<br /><br />I want to understand it, I want to … find some key (11).”<br /><br />I’ve always found that the simple act of writing something down leaves part of you behind. As if the words imbibe part of your personality and if a reader really looks – a truth can be discovered. This was a profound moment in the text for me.<br /><br />I think the other idea that I got from this book that was quite astonishing and startling was that some gens de couleur libre wanted to stay in North America, where the environment was not always in their favour and they did not have the same rights as their white counterparts. I guess, I had always thought – if there was an escape to a place where people would readily respect you, why not take it? But over and over it was reinforced that many of these people felt they had to stay for the future of their people. Who else was going to make the changes happen? This was startling because it was also such an obvious revelation. Of course they had to stay – if they hadn’t, where would we be now?<br /><br />Social structure is hard to go against. Not just because others may oppose you and look down on you if you do, but also because some part of you must break and die before you are able. There was a profound sadness that surrounded each character in this book for this very reason. Cecile, Josette, Colette and Louisa because they didn’t let this happen; Anna Bella, Marie, Marcel, Christophe and Richard because they did. There are things to be admired from both perspectives and also much to be learned from all sides. I deeply appreciate, and am thankful for, the immense strength and many sacrifices of the gens de couleur.<br /><br />There is so much more I could say about how this book affected me and changed me but I would need a vast space and eons of time to express those sentiments. Suffice to say that I finished this book on the third of April and it’s almost May third now. Normally, when I finish a book, the review is up the next day. This book had such a huge impact on me and my life that I had to take time to digest the ramifications before I was able to formulate the words. I believe this book should be used in high school classrooms to promote discussions about gender inequality and racism. I also believe that everybody, and I mean everybody, should read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15245495547074719416" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_552636" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexander Santiago" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexander Santiago" href="/user/show/40104-alexander-santiago">Alexander Santiago</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer552636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer339093913004736222">A beautiful and lush novel set in a very unique community in America in antebellum New Orleans - the gens de couleur libre, the mixed race Creoles of color. The novel, though with many characters who play very important roles in the story, concentrates on the St. Marie family: Cecile St. Marie, the haughty matriarch of dark skin and fine european features who was rescued as a little girl from St. Domingue during the revolt; her daughter, Marie, blessed/cursed with the ability to pass for white, </span>
  <span id="freeText339093913004736222" style="display:none">A beautiful and lush novel set in a very unique community in America in antebellum New Orleans - the gens de couleur libre, the mixed race Creoles of color. The novel, though with many characters who play very important roles in the story, concentrates on the St. Marie family: Cecile St. Marie, the haughty matriarch of dark skin and fine european features who was rescued as a little girl from St. Domingue during the revolt; her daughter, Marie, blessed/cursed with the ability to pass for white, hated and envied by her mother for that ability, and aiming to set her on the path to debut at the city's infamous "quadroon ball"; and Marcel, the honey color complexioned, blue-eyed precocious protagonist who learns very difficult lessons about life while growing into adulthood. Mesmerizing, enchanting, melancholic, overall, a beautiful novel!</span>

<div id="review_33354667" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33354667" />
    <a title="Ronique" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1457184-ronique"><img alt="Ronique" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372459343p2/1457184.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33354667?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronique" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronique" href="/user/show/1457184-ronique">Ronique</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1457184-ronique?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1457184-ronique?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer33354667&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33354667" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8284171777760518057">I know that before I discovered this title, I had already watched Interview with a Vampire (to be reviewed later, btw because Lestat. Yes) and had yet to pick up and read anything by Anne Rice. To be honest, I only noticed this title because of the mini-series on Showtime. I was like, 20 when it debuted and I knew very little to nothing about the gen de couleur libre (I almost typed that without looking it up, four years of French, ftw) and it seemed interesting. It was an entire series about pe</span>
  <span id="freeText8284171777760518057" style="display:none">I know that before I discovered this title, I had already watched Interview with a Vampire (to be reviewed later, btw because Lestat. Yes) and had yet to pick up and read anything by Anne Rice. To be honest, I only noticed this title because of the mini-series on Showtime. I was like, 20 when it debuted and I knew very little to nothing about the gen de couleur libre (I almost typed that without looking it up, four years of French, ftw) and it seemed interesting. It was an entire series about people of color who were not enslaved during a time in American history were the majority of anyone who was not white, were bound by someone who was. I was definitely intrigued. <br /><br />After watching the series, which played out like a dramatic soap opera, I had to find and read the book. It took forever for me to get around to it and the only regret that I had about it was that I hadn't read it sooner. <br /><br />Of course this title doesn't read like an actual historical account on any particular person or family during the time of the gens de couleur, but as a fictional tale about the general plight of these people during pre-Civil War America. They were free but still contained. Marcel, the novel's main protagonist, has to learn this. He has to learn that yes he was raised as the head of his household, being the only male aside from his White-Plantation-Owning father, that did not allow him the same rights and status as a traditional heir has. Marcel grows up believing the world is his and he can have what he wants but, when his father dies and even a bit before then, he is thrown into the cruel and harsh reality of that era.<br /><br />There are other elements to this story. Everyone has a backstory, which is something I love in any novel. The city of New Orleans (because uhm, Anne Rice, hello) has a story within this backdrop as well. <br /><br />Full review/More reviews can be found on my blog at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.ihatecatsbr.com">www.ihatecatsbr.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8284171777760518057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1113203784" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113203784" />
    <a title="Alethea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8633955-alethea"><img alt="Alethea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442471353p2/8633955.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1113203784?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alethea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alethea" href="/user/show/8633955-alethea">Alethea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1113203784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17745266092435121761">The Feast of All Saints is one of the most beautifully written books I have read. The story focuses on the lives of the gens de colour, free people of color in antebellum New Orleans, who created a rich and highly cultured society in the midst of prejudice and the world of slavery. Purely historical fiction, and at times skirting the genre of Southern Gothic, it focuses on young Marcel, the blue-eyed mulatto son of a plantation owner who keeps Marcel's mother and his family in luxury in New Orle</span>
  <span id="freeText17745266092435121761" style="display:none">The Feast of All Saints is one of the most beautifully written books I have read. The story focuses on the lives of the gens de colour, free people of color in antebellum New Orleans, who created a rich and highly cultured society in the midst of prejudice and the world of slavery. Purely historical fiction, and at times skirting the genre of Southern Gothic, it focuses on young Marcel, the blue-eyed mulatto son of a plantation owner who keeps Marcel's mother and his family in luxury in New Orleans, far from his other family. Marcel excels as a student and has been promised life in Paris to continue his studies when he comes of age. Marcel hangs all his hopes upon this dream. His beautiful sister Marie, who could pass as white, loves Richard, a young black man whose family are undertakers, but the culture disdains young girls such as she to marry black men. Families spent a great deal of energy to have their daughters to become mistresses to white men, as Marie and Marcel's mother have done. (This did occur, but from what I read about the subject many of these girls actually settled down as married women within the gens de colour society.) The novel is a slow read, but the details which Anne Rice weaves into the setting creates a world where I felt I had time travelled each evening as I read the book. Marcel's dreams, of course, are dashed, but the novel highlights his search for the true work he is to do as an artist, and so the ending is a triumph.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17745266092435121761" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_23614058" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23614058" />
    <a title="Keri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1209361-keri"><img alt="Keri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343833839p2/1209361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23614058?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keri" href="/user/show/1209361-keri">Keri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23614058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2816117724544548706">as of 6/3/08, this is the most beautiful book I've read! It's Anne Rice so very yummy details. All in all a coming of age story for a "free people of color" family in pre-Civil war era. Time piece is great, the adventure and romance of early Louisiana is so intoxicating. Anne seems to have done a fair amount of research on this book (plus she's lived in New Orleans for quite a while) - according to the brief tours I engaged in while in NOLA, many details match up. Some names and dates are differ</span>
  <span id="freeText2816117724544548706" style="display:none">as of 6/3/08, this is the most beautiful book I've read! It's Anne Rice so very yummy details. All in all a coming of age story for a "free people of color" family in pre-Civil war era. Time piece is great, the adventure and romance of early Louisiana is so intoxicating. Anne seems to have done a fair amount of research on this book (plus she's lived in New Orleans for quite a while) - according to the brief tours I engaged in while in NOLA, many details match up. Some names and dates are different, but it has to be right? I toured NOLA after this book and everything just fell into place - I walked the streets of NOLA just as Marcel and Marie. Each character becomes fully developed, playing intricate roles throughout, but not too hard to follow or throwing the plot off balance. I'm not Anne Rice so I can't put my feelings about this book into words - just read it and fall in love like I have. Ps. this is not a Vampire novel - do not expect long fangs. Also, there is a relationship of varied age-differences that develops which the reader must be forewarned (but this IS Anne Rice).</span>
  <a data-text-id="2816117724544548706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46617964?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmela" href="/user/show/2041238-carmela">Carmela</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46617964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7835924237201712765">This is probably one of my three favorite books by Anne Rice. It is set in New Orleans and is about the life of one man and his three families. His white wife and children, his kept quadroon woman and their children, and his slave woman and their child. This book talks about the complexity of race relations in a very personal way and during a time period when people didn't talk about race at all, 1800s. It is not a ghoulish tale, like Rice is known for writing either. It is a period story about </span>
  <span id="freeText7835924237201712765" style="display:none">This is probably one of my three favorite books by Anne Rice. It is set in New Orleans and is about the life of one man and his three families. His white wife and children, his kept quadroon woman and their children, and his slave woman and their child. This book talks about the complexity of race relations in a very personal way and during a time period when people didn't talk about race at all, 1800s. It is not a ghoulish tale, like Rice is known for writing either. It is a period story about the children of this man and how each position in society played out more in their lives than who their father was in New Orleans. It is an incredible book in my opinion. And in case you are interested my two other favorite books by Anne Rice are The Vampire Lestat and Memnoch the Devil. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7835924237201712765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_50871523" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50871523" />
    <a title="Daniel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2173912-daniel"><img alt="Daniel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587500779p2/2173912.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50871523?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel" href="/user/show/2173912-daniel">Daniel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50871523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6282360075301976807">Let me start by saying that Anne Rice is my favorite author. I discovered her work when I was barely a teenager. Rice painted vivid, metaphysical worlds for her vampires, witches, and spirits. The page turning tales she spun were an escape that brought me through some of the toughest trials of my adolescence. There was one novel, though, that I completely disregarded because it was of the historical fiction genre. The Feast of All Saints is set in Louisiana in the 1840's. The main characters are</span>
  <span id="freeText6282360075301976807" style="display:none">Let me start by saying that Anne Rice is my favorite author. I discovered her work when I was barely a teenager. Rice painted vivid, metaphysical worlds for her vampires, witches, and spirits. The page turning tales she spun were an escape that brought me through some of the toughest trials of my adolescence. There was one novel, though, that I completely disregarded because it was of the historical fiction genre. The Feast of All Saints is set in Louisiana in the 1840's. The main characters are the gens de couleur, or free people of color, in and around New Orleans. I was convinced the book would not interest me for the simple reason that the characters were all mortal.<br /><br />After all these years of neglect I've finally read it and, quite frankly, it has made me re-evaluate her entire body of work. I realize now that it was her characters always that kept me reading. I am a white American, born long after slavery and yet I was able to identify so deeply with the characters in this story that at times I wept. The Feast of All Saints is not about black people or white people or slavery or freedom. It is about the struggles of all people to figure out their identity, their place in the world. And as I look back I understand now that Anne was never really writing about vampires or witches, she was writing about us, about human beings.<br /><br />Unfortunately, this may be the last novel of hers I ever read. After Hurricane Katrina destroyed Anne's beloved New Orleans and much of Louisiana, she turned to Christianity in her grief. Since that time she has written an autobiographical account of her brainwashing, reinterpretations of the Jesus story, and some new rubbish about angels. Don't get me wrong, she has incorporated angels, God, and even the devil in her previous work, but this was always tongue in cheek. The trash she is putting out now is creationist propaganda as far as I can tell. Anne Rice has become the Mel Gibson of the literary world and it is an absolute tragedy. For me, it is as if one of the greatest creative minds of the medium is in a coma.<br /><br />I miss her deeply and can only hope that she returns to us.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6282360075301976807" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <span id="freeText11291124620490496094" style="display:none">This book took a while to get into (it's taken me a month nearly to read!) and I did find that if and when I put it down, I could easily forget about it. (Where as other books have called me to it... and I've ignored the housework to just read, read, read!). <br /><br />I've given it three stars, maybe it deserves two and half. I wasn't sure whether to give it two or three. I did like the story, but like I said, this book wasn't ever begging me to pick it back up. There were places where it was left on a cliff hanger, but not very often. And maybe if I wasn't attempting to read 40 books in a year, I might have just put it aside. However I wanted to read something different than what I had been recently. And this was very different. I'd started, so I'd finish it! <br /><br />Anne Rice is brilliant for her descriptions and her style of writing, but I think, this book being published in 1979, the writing is a little old fashioned. But she does place you in the middle of New Orleans, and you get a good feel for everything around the characters. <br /><br />There is a sort of bitter sweet ending to it. And it's a real eye opener for the slaves, gens de color and the whites in New Orleans in the 19th century. I have actually learnt a little history insight from this book that I wasn't so aware about. It is fiction, but obviously based on the history of that era. <br /><br />It definitely stirred emotions in me. At times it made me feel sad, horrified. <br /><br />If you choose to read this book, and you've been reading 'lighter' material, (before this I was reading Charlaine Harris and I'm going back to her series!) then I say to be patient with it. It's worth reading but some might find it harder going. Get past the first few chapters of this book, and you'll get more into it. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11291124620490496094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_89951689" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/89951689" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1512868-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1269709619p2/1512868.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89951689?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/1512868-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345334534" href="/book/show/6417357-the-feast-of-all-saints">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lisa by: </span>
      Jade Brelsford
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1512868-lisa?shelf=faves">faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1512868-lisa?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1512868-lisa?shelf=hist-fic">hist-fic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1512868-lisa?shelf=book-crushes">book-crushes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1512868-lisa?shelf=been-around-the-world-and-i-i-i">been-around-the-world-and-i-i-i</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89951689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13327504547104008437">Although mostly known for her vampire fiction, Rice's non-paranormal books are easily her best as <i>Cry To Heaven</i> and now this deftly illustrate.<br/><br/>A beautiful mix of history and fiction that plunges us into the incredibly complex lives of the Free People of Colour of New Orleans in the mid 19th century, a world I was largely ignorant of prior to picking this up, I loved this book and soon found myself absorbed completely. Written mostly from the viewpoint of the St Marie family (Cecile, under placag</span>
  <span id="freeText13327504547104008437" style="display:none">Although mostly known for her vampire fiction, Rice's non-paranormal books are easily her best as <i>Cry To Heaven</i> and now this deftly illustrate.<br /><br />A beautiful mix of history and fiction that plunges us into the incredibly complex lives of the Free People of Colour of New Orleans in the mid 19th century, a world I was largely ignorant of prior to picking this up, I loved this book and soon found myself absorbed completely. Written mostly from the viewpoint of the St Marie family (Cecile, under placage with a wealthy white planter, and their two children Marcel and Marie) and the community whose lives touch theirs, the characters within were some of her most vivid to date. From the abhorrent Cecile to the dreamy Marcel, and from the lovely and decent Richard to the scandalous Dolly Rose, there wasn't a single character who I didn't feel intimately acquainted with and invested in their fates (particularly those of Richard and Marie...eep!) Once again New Orleans is easily just as big a character as any of the people within, and Rice writes about it so powerfully you can feel the love for her city flowing from the pages.<br /><br />Gorgeously written, intricately plotted, educational and emotionally powerful, I'd highly recommend this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13327504547104008437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1057767170" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1057767170" />
    <a title="Scott Williams" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15209423-scott-williams"><img alt="Scott Williams" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478435099p2/15209423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1057767170?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott Williams" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott Williams" href="/user/show/15209423-scott-williams">Scott Williams</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1057767170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12868556526217100406">This was my first reading of Anne Rice's second novel. In it, you can clearly see the beginnings of the writer she would become. Here we see the roots of her explorations of historical New Orleans and the multigenerational family storytelling that her Mayfair Witches series would make her famous for.<br/><br/>I love that in 1979, Rice included a gay character in a work of popular fiction without comment. This person is simply present and his romantic entanglements are described as benignly as any others. </span>
  <span id="freeText12868556526217100406" style="display:none">This was my first reading of Anne Rice's second novel. In it, you can clearly see the beginnings of the writer she would become. Here we see the roots of her explorations of historical New Orleans and the multigenerational family storytelling that her Mayfair Witches series would make her famous for.<br /><br />I love that in 1979, Rice included a gay character in a work of popular fiction without comment. This person is simply present and his romantic entanglements are described as benignly as any others. Rice's openness and honesty about sexuality would become another of her trademarks.<br /><br />I'm only giving this book three out of five stars because it didn't capture my attention or imagination as much as other of Rice's works. I feel like the ingredients are all present but they haven't been mixed as successfully as she would manage with subsequent works.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12868556526217100406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText17815576936643759740" style="display:none">Absolutely this is Anne's forgotten masterpiece about self awareness and self discovery.<br />Read it for the first time over more than ten years ago and all I could remember is it was about and a brother and sister and that it made me cry.<br />Yes, it did made me cry again but this time I comprehended all the depth and society analysis within it following the life of the main character in some key years in his life.<br />Free colored population of New Orleans in the early 1800, what an amazing trip around society rules, racism, fear and contempt. And the scariest thing it doesn't feels so far from latin american reality in the 1990s or even now...</span>

<div id="review_180314988" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/180314988" />
    <a title="Roberta Stewart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5607711-roberta-stewart"><img alt="Roberta Stewart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577894768p2/5607711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/180314988?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roberta Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roberta Stewart" href="/user/show/5607711-roberta-stewart">Roberta Stewart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer180314988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7541428898183967780">As I said about "Cry To Heaven" don't dismiss this as just another Anne Rice book. It's an historical novel about being a mixed race or mulatto young man in 19th century New Orleans. There was a whole class of colored, well-off, well-educated and cultured people in New Orleans at this time. They ranked far above the blue-collar Irish immigrants in the complex social strata of the Crescent City. While Anne Rice's writing tends towards the overlush, this is a captivating, interesting story of a ti</span>
  <span id="freeText7541428898183967780" style="display:none">As I said about "Cry To Heaven" don't dismiss this as just another Anne Rice book. It's an historical novel about being a mixed race or mulatto young man in 19th century New Orleans. There was a whole class of colored, well-off, well-educated and cultured people in New Orleans at this time. They ranked far above the blue-collar Irish immigrants in the complex social strata of the Crescent City. While Anne Rice's writing tends towards the overlush, this is a captivating, interesting story of a time in history that many people outside of New Orleans don't know about. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7541428898183967780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5NJnguceAF4FRYKXxY2fhH4/C7s8T0ay3GCbbfVHCBJ+xCDIqxleKGKbPRY+2THLiBYHzTYm3JdeXx/rNI3B/w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('45MQ3ZFBWUYb0t/AiHvTtrOcrwhomFbIZv5ayVLLOxZ5hVeX3UYHMHwMYEFzL335RbWjfmLxzO3kwd5PkwHy+w==')})
  }

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1383250078p3/7577.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice">Anne Rice
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
21,711
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5347672951824225275">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&query=The+Vampire+Chronicles' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice' title='Stan Rice' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold near</span>
  <span id="freeText5347672951824225275" style="display:none">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;query=The+Vampire+Chronicles" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice" title="Stan Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold nearly 100 million copies, making her one of the most widely read authors in modern history.<br /><br />She uses the pseudonym <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17553.Anne_Rampling" rel="nofollow noopener">Anne Rampling</a> for adult-themed fiction (i.e., erotica) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/437669.A_N_Roquelaure" rel="nofollow noopener">A.N. Roquelaure</a> for fiction featuring sexually explicit sado-masochism.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5347672951824225275" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
